❯ /plan
  ⎿  Enabled plan mode

❯ I'm building a Java 17 REST API for a personal task manager as part of a backend engineering assessment. I need you to help me build this thoughtfully and iteratively phase by phase.
  Already Set Up:
  - Spring Boot 3.5.14 with Maven
  - Package: com.project.taskmanager
  - Dependencies: Spring Web, Spring Data JPA, H2, Validation
  - H2 database configured with create-drop mode
  - Server running on port 8080
  - Main application class:TaskmanagerApplication.java

  Architecture I thought of: Controller Layer → Service Layer → Repository Layer → Database (H2)
  My planned package structure:
  In com.project.taskmanager/
  TaskmanagerApplication.java (main file)
  In package controller/ - TaskController.java, AIController.java
  In package service/ - TaskService.java,  AIService.java
  In package repository/ -  TaskRepository.java
  In package model/ - Task.java, Priority.java (enum) , Status.java (enum)
  In package dto/ - TaskRequest.java, TaskResponse.java , AITaskSuggestionRequest.java, AITaskSuggestionResponse.java

  Required Features

  CRUD Endpoints:
  - POST /tasks - Create new task
  - GET /tasks - List all tasks
  - GET /tasks/{id} - Get single task
  - PUT /tasks/{id} - Update task
  - DELETE /tasks/{id} - Delete task

  AI-Powered Endpoint
  - POST /tasks/suggest
    - Accepts a plain-language description
    - Returns a structured task suggestion with title, description, dueDate, priority, and status

  Potential Stretch Features (only if time permits):
  - POST /tasks/{id}/summarize
  - POST /tasks/{id}/breakdown

  Simple UI:
  - Basic HTML page to view tasks, create tasks, and test AI endpoint
  - No fancy styling required - functionality only

  Tests:
  - Unit tests for service layer methods
  - Integration tests for all endpoints
  - Mocked AI endpoint tests

  Edge Cases I found to Handle

  Data Validation:
  - Null/empty title → reject with 400
  - Invalid enum values → reject with 400
  - Due date in the past → reject with 400
  - Description exceeding max length → reject with 400

  API Behavior:
  - GET/PUT/DELETE non-existent task → 404 with meaningful message
  - Malformed JSON → 400 with field-level errors
  - AI API timeout → graceful error message
  - Invalid AI response format → fallback handling

  AI Endpoint Specific:
  - Very vague input ("remind me about stuff") → handle gracefully
  - Missing API key → clear error message
  - Rate limiting scenarios


  I want to build this in phases. Do NOT give me all the code at once.
  For each phase:
  1. I’ll tell you what to build.
  2. You provide complete code for that phase only.
  3. I’ll test it and give feedback.
  4. We iterate if needed.
  5. Then we move to the next phase.

  After each phase, wait for my feedback before moving to the next phase.
  Before writing Phase 1 code, briefly comment on whether this architecture is appropriate for the assessment and suggest only minimal changes if needed.

  Phase 1: Domain Model

  I need you to build this API step by step, starting with the domain model.

  Create a Task entity class, with these specifications:

  Fields:
  - id: Long, auto-generated
  - title: String, required, max 200 characters
  - description: String, optional, max 1000 characters
  - dueDate: LocalDateTime, required, must be in the future
  - priority: enum (LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH), required
  - status: enum (TODO, IN_PROGRESS, DONE), required, defaults to TODO
  - createdAt: LocalDateTime, auto-set on creation
  - updatedAt: LocalDateTime, auto-updated on modification

  Requirements:
  - Use JPA annotations (@Entity, @Table, @Id, @GeneratedValue, etc.)
  - Use Bean Validation annotations (@NotNull, @NotBlank, @Size, @Future)
  - Include a no-args constructor (required by JPA)
  - Include a constructor with all fields except id, createdAt, updatedAt
  - Include explicit getters and setters (don't use Lombok)
  - Create Priority and Status enums as separate files in the model package
  - Use @CreatedDate and @LastModifiedDate for audit fields. If additional auditing configuration is required, explain what should be added and where.

  Provide complete code for:
  1. Task.java - Full entity with all annotations, constructors, getters/setters
  2. Priority.java - Enum with LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH

  Include:

 Plan: Task Manager API — Phase 1: Domain Model

 Context

 Building a Java 17 Spring Boot 3.5.14 REST API for a personal task manager. This is Phase 1 of an iterative assessment build. The goal is to create the JPA entity, two enums, and configure JPA auditing so
 the project compiles and the schema is auto-created by Hibernate on startup.

 Architecture Assessment

 The proposed layered architecture (Controller → Service → Repository → H2) is correct and appropriate for this scope. Two minor notes:
 1. Add @EnableJpaAuditing to TaskmanagerApplication.java — required for @CreatedDate / @LastModifiedDate to populate automatically. This is the only configuration change needed beyond new files.
 2. Plan for a GlobalExceptionHandler (@RestControllerAdvice) in a later phase — the edge cases listed (404, 400, malformed JSON) all route through one.

 No other structural changes needed.

 │ model/Priority.java │ com.project.taskmanager.model │ Enum: LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH                   │
 ├─────────────────────┼────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤

 Key Implementation Details

 Priority.java & Status.java

 - Simple Java enums, no annotations needed on the enum classes themselves.

     Priority.java & Status.java

     - Simple Java enums, no annotations needed on the enum classes themselves.

     Task.java

     - jakarta.persistence.* (not javax.*) — Spring Boot 3 uses Jakarta EE 10.
     - @Enumerated(EnumType.STRING) on both priority and status — stores readable strings in DB instead of ordinal integers.
     - @EntityListeners(AuditingEntityListener.class) — wires the Spring Data auditing listener so @CreatedDate / @LastModifiedDate populate on save.
     - @CreatedDate on createdAt + updatable = false column — prevents Hibernate from overwriting it on updates.
     - @LastModifiedDate on updatedAt — auto-updated on every save.
     - @Future on dueDate — rejects dates in the past at validation time.
     - @Size(max = 200) on title, @Size(max = 1000) on description.
     - @NotBlank on title (rejects null, empty, and whitespace-only).
     - No-args constructor (JPA requirement) + full-fields constructor (excludes id, createdAt, updatedAt).
     - Default status = Status.TODO set in the no-args constructor and full-fields constructor signature defaults.

     TaskmanagerApplication.java modification

     Add @EnableJpaAuditing to enable the auditing infrastructure:
     @SpringBootApplication
     @EnableJpaAuditing
     public class TaskmanagerApplication { ... }

     Verification

     After creating files:
     1. Run ./mvnw spring-boot:run — should start cleanly with no errors.
     2. Visit http://localhost:8080/h2-console, JDBC URL jdbc:h2:mem:taskdb — the TASK table should exist with all columns.
     3. Check column types: PRIORITY and STATUS should be VARCHAR (not INTEGER).
     4. CREATED_AT should appear as a non-nullable timestamp column.
     No endpoints exist yet, so no HTTP testing in Phase 1.

⏺ All four files are done. Here's a summary of what was created and why each decision was made:

  ---
  Architecture note: Your design is solid for this assessment. The only addition you'll need later is a @RestControllerAdvice exception handler class — all your edge cases (404, 400, malformed JSON) funnel
  through one.

  ---
  Files created/modified:

  TaskmanagerApplication.java — Added @EnableJpaAuditing. Without this, @CreatedDate and @LastModifiedDate silently do nothing and the audit columns stay null.

  Priority.java / Status.java — Plain enums. No annotations needed on the enum files themselves; the @Enumerated(EnumType.STRING) lives on the entity field.

  Task.java — Key decisions:
  - jakarta.persistence.* (not javax.*) — Spring Boot 3 dropped the old namespace
  - @EntityListeners(AuditingEntityListener.class) — wires the auditing listener to this entity
  - @Column(updatable = false) on createdAt — Hibernate won't touch it after initial insert
  - @Enumerated(EnumType.STRING) on both enums — stores "HIGH" not 2 in the DB, making the H2 console readable and migrations safer
  - No-args constructor defaults status = TODO so it's never null if someone calls new Task()

❯ I noticed a potential issue with @Future on Task.dueDate.

  If a task becomes overdue, then later PUT requests could fail validation even if the user is only trying to:
  mark the task as DONE
  update the description
  change the priority

  I want to avoid overengineering with validation groups unless truly necessary.

  Would it be better to:
  1. Keep @Future as-is

✻ Brewed for 22m 43s

❯ I noticed a potential issue with @Future on Task.dueDate.

  If a task becomes overdue, then later PUT requests could fail validation even if the user is only trying to:
  mark the task as DONE
  update the description
  change the priority

  I want to avoid overengineering with validation groups unless truly necessary.

  Would it be better to:
  1. Keep @Future as-is
  2. Remove @Future from the entity and validate future dates only during task creation/business logic
  3. Use separate validation behavior for create vs update operations

  Please recommend the simplest maintainable approach for this assessment scope and explain the tradeoffs before we move to Phase 2.


⏺ Good catch — this is a real problem worth solving now. Here's the tradeoff breakdown:

  Option 1 (keep @Future on entity): Breaks on any PUT to an overdue task. Not workable.

  Option 3 (validation groups): Solves it correctly but adds marker interfaces, @Validated(OnCreate.class) on controllers, and group-aware annotations. Overkill for this scope, and you already said so.

  Option 2 (remove from entity, validate elsewhere): This is the right call — but the where matters. The cleanest place is the DTO, not the service.

  My recommendation: remove @Future from the entity, put it on TaskRequest only.

  The entity is a persistence object — it represents what's in the database, including overdue tasks. Validation belongs at the API boundary, which is the DTO. When you build TaskRequest in Phase 3:

  - POST /tasks uses TaskRequest with @Future on dueDate → creation rejects past dates
  - PUT /tasks/{id} — for update, the service checks isBefore(now()) only if dueDate is being changed, allowing status/description/priority updates on overdue tasks with no friction

  This keeps the validation declarative for creation and makes the update behavior explicit in one readable service method. No groups, no duplicated DTOs.

⏺ Both files created. A few design notes worth calling out:

  buildError private helper — centralizes the response shape so all four handlers produce identical structure. The errors key is only included when non-null, so 404/500 responses stay clean:

  // 404
  { "timestamp": "...", "status": 404, "message": "Task not found with id: 5" }

  // 400 validation
  { "timestamp": "...", "status": 400, "message": "Validation failed",
    "errors": { "title": "Title is required", "dueDate": "Due date must be in the future" } }

  putIfAbsent for field errors — if Bean Validation fires multiple constraint violations on the same field, only the first message is kept. This avoids cluttering the response with redundant messages for the
  same field.

  HttpMessageNotReadableException — covers two cases with one handler: completely malformed JSON (syntax error) and a valid JSON structure with an unrecognized enum value (e.g., "priority": "URGENT"). Spring
  wraps both as HttpMessageNotReadableException, so one handler is sufficient.

  Exception catch-all — intentionally generic message to avoid leaking internal details to clients. Stack traces remain in server logs.

  Ready for Phase 5 (Service layer) when you are.

  Phase 5: TaskService

  Create the service layer with business logic for CRUD operations.

    - Map TaskRequest to Task entity
    - Default status to TODO if null
    - Save the task
    - Map saved Task entity to TaskResponse

  - getAllTasks() → List<TaskResponse>
    - Return all tasks from repository mapped to TaskResponse

  - getTaskById(Long id) → TaskResponse
    - Find task by ID
    - Throw TaskNotFoundException if not found
    - Map Task to TaskResponse

  - updateTask(Long id, TaskRequest request) → TaskResponse
    - Find existing task or throw TaskNotFoundException
    - If dueDate is being changed AND the new date is in the past, reject it
    - Allow updating overdue tasks when only changing status/description/priority
    - Update fields from request
    - Default status to TODO if null
    - Save updated task
    - Map saved Task to TaskResponse

  - deleteTask(Long id) → void
    - Find task or throw TaskNotFoundException
    - Delete the task

⏺ Done. A few things worth noting:

  GlobalExceptionHandler update — IllegalArgumentException now maps to 400 with the service's message passed through directly. This is safe because those messages are authored by us, not user input, so
  there's no risk of leaking internals.

  createTask — why duplicate the @Future check? The @Future on TaskRequest fires at the controller boundary when @Valid is used. The service check (isAfter(now())) makes the service self-contained and
  directly testable without a web layer (useful in unit tests). Both guard the same invariant from different entry points.

  updateTask — the due-date logic: The dueDateChanged flag is the core of the strategy we agreed on. Sending the same past dueDate (e.g. to mark a task DONE) passes through cleanly. Sending a new past date is
   rejected. Sending any future date is always allowed.

  deleteTask — findById + delete vs existsById + deleteById: Using findById is consistent with the other methods and avoids a race between the existence check and the delete call.

  Controller note for Phase 6: For the PUT /tasks/{id} endpoint, do not use @Valid on the request body. The @Future annotation on TaskRequest.dueDate would reject any PUT request for an overdue task, even if
  the client is only changing status. Bean Validation for other fields (@NotBlank, @Size) will need to be enforced by the service or a manual check. We can discuss the cleanest approach when we get there.

  Ready for Phase 6 (Controller layer) when you are.

  Now Phase 6: TaskController

  Create a REST controller with CRUD endpoints.

  Package: com.project.taskmanager.controller

  Create TaskController with these endpoints:
  - POST /tasks → createTask
  - GET /tasks → getAllTasks
  - GET /tasks/{id} → getTaskById
  - PUT /tasks/{id} → updateTask
  - DELETE /tasks/{id} → deleteTask

  Requirements:
  - Use @RestController
  - Base path should be /tasks
  - Inject TaskService via constructor
  - POST should use @Valid on TaskRequest and return 201 Created
  - PUT should NOT use @Valid on TaskRequest because service handles update-specific validation
  - GET endpoints should return 200 OK
  - DELETE should return 204 No Content
  - Use ResponseEntity for clear status codes
  - Include JavaDoc comments

  Provide complete code for TaskController.java only.

⏺ Done. The controller is intentionally thin — no logic, just HTTP mapping and delegation to the service.

  A few notes:

  Status codes: POST returns 201 via ResponseEntity.status(HttpStatus.CREATED). DELETE returns 204 via ResponseEntity.noContent().build(). GETs and PUT return 200 via ResponseEntity.ok(). 404 and 400 are
  handled transparently by GlobalExceptionHandler — no try/catch needed here.

  @Valid on POST only — as agreed. The comment on updateTask documents the deliberate omission so the next reader doesn't "fix" it.

  @PathVariable Long id — Spring will reject non-numeric IDs (e.g. /tasks/abc) with a 400 before the controller method is even invoked, handled by the HttpMessageNotReadableException / general exception
  handler.

  At this point the core CRUD stack is complete end-to-end. You can verify the full happy path now:

  # Start the server
  ./mvnw spring-boot:run

  # Create a task
  curl -s -X POST http://localhost:8080/tasks \
    -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
    -d '{"title":"Test task","dueDate":"2027-01-01T10:00:00","priority":"HIGH"}' | jq

  # List tasks
  curl -s http://localhost:8080/tasks | jq

  # Get by ID
  curl -s http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 | jq

  # Update
  curl -s -X PUT http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 \
    -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
    -d '{"title":"Updated","dueDate":"2027-01-01T10:00:00","priority":"LOW","status":"DONE"}' | jq

  # Delete
  curl -s -X DELETE http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}"

❯ Phase 6 complete. All CRUD endpoints working, including overdue-task edge case.

  Phase 7: AI-Powered Task Suggestion
  Architectural Decision: I want to implement the AI integration using a provider-based architecture with an AIProvider interface rather than a single concrete AIService.
  This allows:
  - Easy swapping between AI models (Gemini, Claude, GPT-4) without changing controller code - Better testability (can mock the provider interface)
  - Follows Dependency Inversion Principle
  - Keeps the external AI integration isolated if we later add fallback providers or switch models.
  Keep the provider abstraction lightweight - do not add extra factories or unnecessary configuration classes.
  Create an AI endpoint with a provider-based architecture:
  Endpoint: POST /tasks/suggest

  Configuration:
  - application.properties contains: gemini.api.key=${GEMINI_API_KEY}
  - I have my Gemini API key ready
  - I'll provide it via IntelliJ environment variable: GEMINI_API_KEY

  Create these files:
  - dto/AITaskSuggestionRequest.java
  - dto/AITaskSuggestionResponse.java
  - service/AIProvider.java (interface)
  - service/GeminiAIService.java (implements AIProvider)
  - service/AIService.java (facade that uses AIProvider)
  - controller/AIController.java

  AITaskSuggestionRequest:
  - description: String, @NotBlank, @Size(max=1000)

  AITaskSuggestionResponse:
  - suggestedTask: TaskRequest
  - reasoning: String

  AIProvider interface:
  - Single method: suggestTask(String description) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - This interface allows swapping AI providers (Gemini, Claude, GPT-4) without changing controller/service code

  GeminiAIService (implements AIProvider):
  - @Service annotation
  - @Value("${gemini.api.key}") to inject API key
  - Use Java 17 HttpClient
  - Use Jackson ObjectMapper
  - Gemini API endpoint: https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models/gemini-1.5-flash:generateContent?key={apiKey}
  - HTTP POST with Content-Type: application/json
  - Request body should ask Gemini to return ONLY valid JSON with:
    - title
    - description
    - dueDate (ISO LocalDateTime format, e.g., 2026-12-20T18:00:00)
    - priority (LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH)
    - status (TODO)
    - reasoning (brief explanation)
  - Parse Gemini response from: candidates[0].content.parts[0].text
  - Strip markdown code fences if present (```json...```)
  - Error handling:
    - Missing API key → IllegalArgumentException
    - Non-200 responses → include status code and response body for debugging
    - Timeout/interrupted → handle gracefully
    - Malformed JSON → clear error message

  AIService:
  - @Service annotation
  - Constructor-inject AIProvider
  - Single method: generateTaskSuggestion(AITaskSuggestionRequest request) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - Delegates to AIProvider.suggestTask()
  - This layer allows adding cross-cutting concerns later (logging, caching, fallback providers)

  AIController:
  - @RestController
  - Base path: /tasks
  - POST /suggest
  - @Valid AITaskSuggestionRequest
  - Inject AIService
  - Return 200 OK with AITaskSuggestionResponse

  Important:
  - Does NOT persist to database
  - Returns suggestion only
  - Use regular classes
  - Include constructors, getters/setters, imports, JavaDoc
  - Single method: generateTaskSuggestion(AITaskSuggestionRequest request) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - Delegates to AIProvider.suggestTask()
  - This layer allows adding cross-cutting concerns later (logging, caching, fallback providers)

  AIController:

  - Base path: /tasks
  - POST /suggest
  - @Valid AITaskSuggestionRequest

  - Return 200 OK with AITaskSuggestionResponse

  Important:

⏺ All 6 files created. Key design decisions worth noting:

  buildRequestBody uses ObjectMapper for the Gemini request body — not string interpolation. This safely escapes the user's description as a JSON string value, so input like "remind me about John's
  "important" meeting" can't break the JSON structure.

  parseGeminiResponse uses root.at("/candidates/0/content/parts/0/text") — the at() method returns MissingNode (not null) if the path doesn't exist, so .asText() safely returns an empty string rather than
  throwing NPE. If Gemini changes its response shape, the parse step will fail with a meaningful error.

  stripCodeFences — despite the prompt saying "no code fences", Gemini 1.5-flash frequently ignores this. The regex ^```(?:json)?\\s* handles both  ```json and plain ``` openings.

  InterruptedException handling — re-sets the interrupt flag with Thread.currentThread().interrupt() before throwing. This is the correct pattern; swallowing the flag silently breaks thread pools.

  application.properties — already had gemini.api.key=${GEMINI_API_KEY} at line 25, so no change needed there.

⏺ All three test files created. A few things worth noting before you run them:

  TaskServiceTest — createdAt and updatedAt are not asserted on because @CreatedDate/@LastModifiedDate only fire through the full JPA stack. The service's toResponse() will map them as null in unit tests,
  which is correct and expected.

  TaskControllerIntegrationTest — three design decisions:
  - @TestPropertySource(properties = "gemini.api.key=test-key") lets the Spring context start — the GeminiAIService constructor won't throw because "test-key" is non-blank. No real Gemini calls are made since
   no test hits /tasks/suggest.
  - taskRepository.deleteAll() in @BeforeEach gives each test a clean H2 slate regardless of execution order.
  - TaskResponse is intentionally immutable (no setters/no-args constructor), so all response assertions use Map.class deserialization instead. This is the correct pattern for testing immutable outbound DTOs
  without modifying their design.

  AIServiceTest — uses assertSame rather than assertEquals to verify that AIService passes the mock's return value through unchanged (reference identity is exactly what we're testing here).

  Run with:
  ./mvnw test

  Ready for Phase 9 when you are.

⏺ All three test files created. A few things worth noting before you run them:

  TaskServiceTest — createdAt and updatedAt are not asserted on because @CreatedDate/@LastModifiedDate only fire through the full JPA stack. The service's toResponse() will map them as null in unit tests,
  which is correct and expected.

  TaskControllerIntegrationTest — three design decisions:
  - @TestPropertySource(properties = "gemini.api.key=test-key") lets the Spring context start — the GeminiAIService constructor won't throw because "test-key" is non-blank. No real Gemini calls are made since
  - taskRepository.deleteAll() in @BeforeEach gives each test a clean H2 slate regardless of execution order.
  - TaskResponse is intentionally immutable (no setters/no-args constructor), so all response assertions use Map.class deserialization instead. This is the correct pattern for testing immutable outbound DTOs
  without modifying their design.

  AIServiceTest — uses assertSame rather than assertEquals to verify that AIService passes the mock's return value through unchanged (reference identity is exactly what we're testing here).

  Run with:
  ./mvnw test

⏺ Done. A few design decisions worth noting:

  datetime-local → API compatibility — the input produces "2027-06-15T09:00" (no seconds). Spring's JavaTimeModule deserializer uses ISO_LOCAL_DATE_TIME which has optional seconds, so this format parses
  correctly without any server changes.

  useAiSuggestion() — when the user clicks "Fill Create Form With This Suggestion", it populates all create-form fields from the AI response, strips seconds from dueDate with .substring(0, 16) to match what
  datetime-local expects, then smooth-scrolls to the form. The user can review and tweak before submitting.

  XSS prevention — all user-supplied text rendered into the table goes through esc(), which uses the DOM createTextNode trick rather than regex replacement. This is injection-safe.

  Error display — formatError() handles both field-level validation error maps (e.g. {title: "Title is required"}) and simple message strings, so all four error shapes from GlobalExceptionHandler display
  meaningfully.

  Visit http://localhost:8080 after starting the server to test it.

  Ready for Phase 10 when you are.

⏺ Done. Here's a summary of every change made:

  HTML changes:
  - novalidate added to <form> — suppresses all browser native popups
  - required removed from inputs (redundant now that JS owns validation)
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-title"> added after title input
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-dueDate"> added after dueDate input
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-ai-desc"> added after AI description textarea
  - .field-err CSS: color: red; font-size: 0.85em; display: block; margin-left: 114px — aligns under the input, not the label

  JS changes:
  - showFieldError(fieldId, message) / clearFieldError(fieldId) / clearAllFieldErrors() — reusable helpers that find err-{fieldId} spans
  - validateCreateForm() — checks title not blank, dueDate not blank, dueDate strictly after new Date() — returns false and shows inline errors if any fail
  - createTask() — calls clearAllFieldErrors() then validateCreateForm() and bails early if invalid; .trim() on title before sending so a whitespace-only title that slips through still gets caught server-side
  - resetCreateForm() — now also calls clearAllFieldErrors()
  - suggestTask() — uses showFieldError('ai-desc', ...) instead of the old setMsg approach for the empty-description case
  - useAiSuggestion() — calls clearAllFieldErrors() when populating the form
  - Three addEventListener('input', ...) calls — clears the relevant field's error the moment the user starts correcting it

 Key Implementation Details

 Priority.java & Status.java

 - Simple Java enums, no annotations needed on the enum classes themselves.

     Priority.java & Status.java

     - Simple Java enums, no annotations needed on the enum classes themselves.

     Task.java

     - jakarta.persistence.* (not javax.*) — Spring Boot 3 uses Jakarta EE 10.
     - @Enumerated(EnumType.STRING) on both priority and status — stores readable strings in DB instead of ordinal integers.
     - @EntityListeners(AuditingEntityListener.class) — wires the Spring Data auditing listener so @CreatedDate / @LastModifiedDate populate on save.
     - @CreatedDate on createdAt + updatable = false column — prevents Hibernate from overwriting it on updates.
     - @LastModifiedDate on updatedAt — auto-updated on every save.
     - @Future on dueDate — rejects dates in the past at validation time.
     - @Size(max = 200) on title, @Size(max = 1000) on description.
     - @NotBlank on title (rejects null, empty, and whitespace-only).
     - No-args constructor (JPA requirement) + full-fields constructor (excludes id, createdAt, updatedAt).
     - Default status = Status.TODO set in the no-args constructor and full-fields constructor signature defaults.

     TaskmanagerApplication.java modification

     Add @EnableJpaAuditing to enable the auditing infrastructure:
     @SpringBootApplication
     @EnableJpaAuditing
     public class TaskmanagerApplication { ... }

✻ Brewed for 22m 43s

❯ I noticed a potential issue with @Future on Task.dueDate.

  If a task becomes overdue, then later PUT requests could fail validation even if the user is only trying to:
  mark the task as DONE
  update the description
  change the priority

  I want to avoid overengineering with validation groups unless truly necessary.

  Would it be better to:
  1. Keep @Future as-is
  2. Remove @Future from the entity and validate future dates only during task creation/business logic
  3. Use separate validation behavior for create vs update operations

  Please recommend the simplest maintainable approach for this assessment scope and explain the tradeoffs before we move to Phase 2.


⏺ Good catch — this is a real problem worth solving now. Here's the tradeoff breakdown:

  Option 1 (keep @Future on entity): Breaks on any PUT to an overdue task. Not workable.

  Option 3 (validation groups): Solves it correctly but adds marker interfaces, @Validated(OnCreate.class) on controllers, and group-aware annotations. Overkill for this scope, and you already said so.

  Option 2 (remove from entity, validate elsewhere): This is the right call — but the where matters. The cleanest place is the DTO, not the service.

  My recommendation: remove @Future from the entity, put it on TaskRequest only.

  The entity is a persistence object — it represents what's in the database, including overdue tasks. Validation belongs at the API boundary, which is the DTO. When you build TaskRequest in Phase 3:

  - POST /tasks uses TaskRequest with @Future on dueDate → creation rejects past dates
  - PUT /tasks/{id} — for update, the service checks isBefore(now()) only if dueDate is being changed, allowing status/description/priority updates on overdue tasks with no friction

  This keeps the validation declarative for creation and makes the update behavior explicit in one readable service method. No groups, no duplicated DTOs.


⏺ Good catch — this is a real problem worth solving now. Here's the tradeoff breakdown:

  Option 1 (keep @Future on entity): Breaks on any PUT to an overdue task. Not workable.

  Option 3 (validation groups): Solves it correctly but adds marker interfaces, @Validated(OnCreate.class) on controllers, and group-aware annotations. Overkill for this scope, and you already said so.

  Option 2 (remove from entity, validate elsewhere): This is the right call — but the where matters. The cleanest place is the DTO, not the service.

  Phase 4: Exception Handling

⏺ Both files created. A few design notes worth calling out:

  buildError private helper — centralizes the response shape so all four handlers produce identical structure. The errors key is only included when non-null, so 404/500 responses stay clean:

  // 404
  { "timestamp": "...", "status": 404, "message": "Task not found with id: 5" }

  // 400 validation
  { "timestamp": "...", "status": 400, "message": "Validation failed",
    "errors": { "title": "Title is required", "dueDate": "Due date must be in the future" } }

  putIfAbsent for field errors — if Bean Validation fires multiple constraint violations on the same field, only the first message is kept. This avoids cluttering the response with redundant messages for the
  same field.

  HttpMessageNotReadableException — covers two cases with one handler: completely malformed JSON (syntax error) and a valid JSON structure with an unrecognized enum value (e.g., "priority": "URGENT"). Spring
  wraps both as HttpMessageNotReadableException, so one handler is sufficient.

  Exception catch-all — intentionally generic message to avoid leaking internal details to clients. Stack traces remain in server logs.

  Ready for Phase 5 (Service layer) when you are.

  Phase 5: TaskService

  Create the service layer with business logic for CRUD operations.

  Package: com.project.taskmanager.service

  Create TaskService class with these specifications:

  Required methods:
  - createTask(TaskRequest request) → TaskResponse
    - Validate dueDate is in the future
    - Map TaskRequest to Task entity
    - Default status to TODO if null
    - Save the task
    - Map saved Task entity to TaskResponse

  - getAllTasks() → List<TaskResponse>
    - Return all tasks from repository mapped to TaskResponse

  - getTaskById(Long id) → TaskResponse
    - Find task by ID
    - Throw TaskNotFoundException if not found
    - Map Task to TaskResponse

  - updateTask(Long id, TaskRequest request) → TaskResponse
    - Find existing task or throw TaskNotFoundException
    - If dueDate is being changed AND the new date is in the past, reject it
    - Allow updating overdue tasks when only changing status/description/priority
    - Update fields from request
    - Default status to TODO if null
    - Save updated task
    - Map saved Task to TaskResponse

  - deleteTask(Long id) → void
    - Find task or throw TaskNotFoundException
    - Delete the task

  Requirements:
  - Use @Service annotation
  - Inject TaskRepository via constructor
  - Use private helper method to map Task → TaskResponse
  - Handle the dueDate validation edge case we discussed earlier

⏺ Done. A few things worth noting:

  GlobalExceptionHandler update — IllegalArgumentException now maps to 400 with the service's message passed through directly. This is safe because those messages are authored by us, not user input, so
  there's no risk of leaking internals.

  createTask — why duplicate the @Future check? The @Future on TaskRequest fires at the controller boundary when @Valid is used. The service check (isAfter(now())) makes the service self-contained and
  directly testable without a web layer (useful in unit tests). Both guard the same invariant from different entry points.

  updateTask — the due-date logic: The dueDateChanged flag is the core of the strategy we agreed on. Sending the same past dueDate (e.g. to mark a task DONE) passes through cleanly. Sending a new past date is
   rejected. Sending any future date is always allowed.

  deleteTask — findById + delete vs existsById + deleteById: Using findById is consistent with the other methods and avoids a race between the existence check and the delete call.

  Controller note for Phase 6: For the PUT /tasks/{id} endpoint, do not use @Valid on the request body. The @Future annotation on TaskRequest.dueDate would reject any PUT request for an overdue task, even if
  the client is only changing status. Bean Validation for other fields (@NotBlank, @Size) will need to be enforced by the service or a manual check. We can discuss the cleanest approach when we get there.

  Ready for Phase 6 (Controller layer) when you are.

⏺ Done. The controller is intentionally thin — no logic, just HTTP mapping and delegation to the service.

  A few notes:

  Status codes: POST returns 201 via ResponseEntity.status(HttpStatus.CREATED). DELETE returns 204 via ResponseEntity.noContent().build(). GETs and PUT return 200 via ResponseEntity.ok(). 404 and 400 are
  handled transparently by GlobalExceptionHandler — no try/catch needed here.

  @Valid on POST only — as agreed. The comment on updateTask documents the deliberate omission so the next reader doesn't "fix" it.

  @PathVariable Long id — Spring will reject non-numeric IDs (e.g. /tasks/abc) with a 400 before the controller method is even invoked, handled by the HttpMessageNotReadableException / general exception
  handler.

  At this point the core CRUD stack is complete end-to-end. You can verify the full happy path now:

  # Start the server
  ./mvnw spring-boot:run

  # Create a task
  curl -s -X POST http://localhost:8080/tasks \
    -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
    -d '{"title":"Test task","dueDate":"2027-01-01T10:00:00","priority":"HIGH"}' | jq

  # List tasks
  curl -s http://localhost:8080/tasks | jq

  # Get by ID
  curl -s http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 | jq

  # Update
  curl -s -X PUT http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 \
    -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
    -d '{"title":"Updated","dueDate":"2027-01-01T10:00:00","priority":"LOW","status":"DONE"}' | jq

  # Delete
  curl -s -X DELETE http://localhost:8080/tasks/1 -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}"

❯ Phase 6 complete. All CRUD endpoints working, including overdue-task edge case.

  Phase 7: AI-Powered Task Suggestion
  Architectural Decision: I want to implement the AI integration using a provider-based architecture with an AIProvider interface rather than a single concrete AIService.
  This allows:
  - Easy swapping between AI models (Gemini, Claude, GPT-4) without changing controller code - Better testability (can mock the provider interface)
  - Follows Dependency Inversion Principle
  - Keeps the external AI integration isolated if we later add fallback providers or switch models.
  Keep the provider abstraction lightweight - do not add extra factories or unnecessary configuration classes.
  Create an AI endpoint with a provider-based architecture:
  Endpoint: POST /tasks/suggest

  Configuration:
  - application.properties contains: gemini.api.key=${GEMINI_API_KEY}
  - I have my Gemini API key ready
  - I'll provide it via IntelliJ environment variable: GEMINI_API_KEY

  Create these files:
  - dto/AITaskSuggestionRequest.java
  - dto/AITaskSuggestionResponse.java
  - service/AIProvider.java (interface)
  - service/GeminiAIService.java (implements AIProvider)
  - service/AIService.java (facade that uses AIProvider)
  - controller/AIController.java

  AITaskSuggestionRequest:
  - description: String, @NotBlank, @Size(max=1000)

  AITaskSuggestionResponse:
  - suggestedTask: TaskRequest
  - reasoning: String

  AIProvider interface:
  - Single method: suggestTask(String description) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - This interface allows swapping AI providers (Gemini, Claude, GPT-4) without changing controller/service code

  GeminiAIService (implements AIProvider):
  - @Service annotation
  - @Value("${gemini.api.key}") to inject API key
  - Use Java 17 HttpClient
  - Use Jackson ObjectMapper
  - Gemini API endpoint: https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models/gemini-1.5-flash:generateContent?key={apiKey}
  - HTTP POST with Content-Type: application/json
  - Request body should ask Gemini to return ONLY valid JSON with:
    - title
    - description
    - dueDate (ISO LocalDateTime format, e.g., 2026-12-20T18:00:00)
    - priority (LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH)
    - status (TODO)
    - reasoning (brief explanation)
  - Parse Gemini response from: candidates[0].content.parts[0].text
  - Strip markdown code fences if present (```json...```)
  - Error handling:
    - Missing API key → IllegalArgumentException
    - Non-200 responses → include status code and response body for debugging
    - Timeout/interrupted → handle gracefully
    - Malformed JSON → clear error message

  AIService:
  - @Service annotation
  - Constructor-inject AIProvider
  - Single method: generateTaskSuggestion(AITaskSuggestionRequest request) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - Delegates to AIProvider.suggestTask()
  - This layer allows adding cross-cutting concerns later (logging, caching, fallback providers)

  AIController:
  - @RestController
  - Base path: /tasks
  - POST /suggest
  - @Valid AITaskSuggestionRequest
  - Inject AIService
  - Return 200 OK with AITaskSuggestionResponse

  Important:
  - Does NOT persist to database
  - Returns suggestion only
  - Use regular classes
  - Include constructors, getters/setters, imports, JavaDoc
  - Single method: generateTaskSuggestion(AITaskSuggestionRequest request) → AITaskSuggestionResponse
  - Delegates to AIProvider.suggestTask()
  - This layer allows adding cross-cutting concerns later (logging, caching, fallback providers)

⏺ All 6 files created. Key design decisions worth noting:

  buildRequestBody uses ObjectMapper for the Gemini request body — not string interpolation. This safely escapes the user's description as a JSON string value, so input like "remind me about John's
  "important" meeting" can't break the JSON structure.

  parseGeminiResponse uses root.at("/candidates/0/content/parts/0/text") — the at() method returns MissingNode (not null) if the path doesn't exist, so .asText() safely returns an empty string rather than
  throwing NPE. If Gemini changes its response shape, the parse step will fail with a meaningful error.

  stripCodeFences — despite the prompt saying "no code fences", Gemini 1.5-flash frequently ignores this. The regex ^```(?:json)?\\s* handles both  ```json and plain ``` openings.

  InterruptedException handling — re-sets the interrupt flag with Thread.currentThread().interrupt() before throwing. This is the correct pattern; swallowing the flag silently breaks thread pools.

  application.properties — already had gemini.api.key=${GEMINI_API_KEY} at line 25, so no change needed there.

⏺ All three test files created. A few things worth noting before you run them:

  TaskServiceTest — createdAt and updatedAt are not asserted on because @CreatedDate/@LastModifiedDate only fire through the full JPA stack. The service's toResponse() will map them as null in unit tests,
  which is correct and expected.

  TaskControllerIntegrationTest — three design decisions:
  - @TestPropertySource(properties = "gemini.api.key=test-key") lets the Spring context start — the GeminiAIService constructor won't throw because "test-key" is non-blank. No real Gemini calls are made since
   no test hits /tasks/suggest.
  - taskRepository.deleteAll() in @BeforeEach gives each test a clean H2 slate regardless of execution order.
  - TaskResponse is intentionally immutable (no setters/no-args constructor), so all response assertions use Map.class deserialization instead. This is the correct pattern for testing immutable outbound DTOs
  without modifying their design.

  AIServiceTest — uses assertSame rather than assertEquals to verify that AIService passes the mock's return value through unchanged (reference identity is exactly what we're testing here).

  Run with:
  ./mvnw test

  Ready for Phase 9 when you are.

⏺ All three test files created. A few things worth noting before you run them:

  TaskServiceTest — createdAt and updatedAt are not asserted on because @CreatedDate/@LastModifiedDate only fire through the full JPA stack. The service's toResponse() will map them as null in unit tests,
  which is correct and expected.

  TaskControllerIntegrationTest — three design decisions:
  - @TestPropertySource(properties = "gemini.api.key=test-key") lets the Spring context start — the GeminiAIService constructor won't throw because "test-key" is non-blank. No real Gemini calls are made since
  - taskRepository.deleteAll() in @BeforeEach gives each test a clean H2 slate regardless of execution order.
  - TaskResponse is intentionally immutable (no setters/no-args constructor), so all response assertions use Map.class deserialization instead. This is the correct pattern for testing immutable outbound DTOs

⏺ Done. A few design decisions worth noting:

  datetime-local → API compatibility — the input produces "2027-06-15T09:00" (no seconds). Spring's JavaTimeModule deserializer uses ISO_LOCAL_DATE_TIME which has optional seconds, so this format parses
  correctly without any server changes.

  useAiSuggestion() — when the user clicks "Fill Create Form With This Suggestion", it populates all create-form fields from the AI response, strips seconds from dueDate with .substring(0, 16) to match what
  datetime-local expects, then smooth-scrolls to the form. The user can review and tweak before submitting.

  XSS prevention — all user-supplied text rendered into the table goes through esc(), which uses the DOM createTextNode trick rather than regex replacement. This is injection-safe.

  Error display — formatError() handles both field-level validation error maps (e.g. {title: "Title is required"}) and simple message strings, so all four error shapes from GlobalExceptionHandler display
  meaningfully.

  Visit http://localhost:8080 after starting the server to test it.

  Ready for Phase 10 when you are.

  correctly without any server changes.

  datetime-local expects, then smooth-scrolls to the form. The user can review and tweak before submitting.

  meaningfully.

⏺ Done. Here's a summary of every change made:

  HTML changes:
  - novalidate added to <form> — suppresses all browser native popups
  - required removed from inputs (redundant now that JS owns validation)
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-title"> added after title input
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-dueDate"> added after dueDate input
  - <span class="field-err" id="err-ai-desc"> added after AI description textarea

  JS changes:
  - showFieldError(fieldId, message) / clearFieldError(fieldId) / clearAllFieldErrors() — reusable helpers that find err-{fieldId} spans
  - validateCreateForm() — checks title not blank, dueDate not blank, dueDate strictly after new Date() — returns false and shows inline errors if any fail
  - createTask() — calls clearAllFieldErrors() then validateCreateForm() and bails early if invalid; .trim() on title before sending so a whitespace-only title that slips through still gets caught server-side
  - resetCreateForm() — now also calls clearAllFieldErrors()
  - suggestTask() — uses showFieldError('ai-desc', ...) instead of the old setMsg approach for the empty-description case
  - useAiSuggestion() — calls clearAllFieldErrors() when populating the form
  - Three addEventListener('input', ...) calls — clears the relevant field's error the moment the user starts correcting it

❯ Add filtering and sorting capabilities to the task management API and UI.

  IMPLEMENTATION APPROACH:
  Keep this implementation simple and assessment-focused. Since this is an in-memory H2 task manager with no pagination requirement, implement filtering/sorting in the service layer using Java streams and
  comparators. Do not add complex custom queries or specifications.

  BACKEND CHANGES:

  1. TaskRepository:
     - No changes needed (keep existing JpaRepository<Task, Long>)

  2. TaskService:
     - Add method: getAllTasks(Status status, Priority priority, String sortBy, String sortOrder)
     - All parameters optional (nullable)
     - Fetch all tasks from repository
     - Filter using streams (filter by status if provided, filter by priority if provided)
     - Sort using Comparator (sortBy: dueDate, priority, createdAt, title)
     - VALIDATION: If sortBy is null/blank or unsupported, use default "createdAt"
     - VALIDATION: If sortOrder is null/blank or unsupported, use default "desc"
     - Default sort: createdAt descending (newest first)
     - Return List<TaskResponse>

  3. TaskController GET /tasks endpoint:
     - Add query parameters: status, priority, sortBy, sortOrder
     - All optional using @RequestParam(required = false)
     - Example: GET /tasks?status=TODO&priority=HIGH&sortBy=dueDate&sortOrder=asc
     - Delegate to updated service method

  FRONTEND CHANGES:

  4. Add filtering UI above the task table:
     - Dropdown for Status filter (All, TODO, IN_PROGRESS, DONE)
     - Dropdown for Priority filter (All, LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH)
     - Dropdown for Sort By (Due Date, Priority, Created, Title)
     - Dropdown for Sort Order (Ascending, Descending)
     - Apply Filters button
     - Clear Filters button (resets to default view)

     - Modify loadTasks() function to accept optional filter/sort parameters
     - Build query string from selected dropdown values
     - Send GET request to /tasks with query parameters
     - Wire up Apply Filters and Clear Filters buttons
     - IMPORTANT: Preserve current filters when refreshing after create/edit/delete operations
     - Store current filter state and reapply it when loadTasks() is called after CRUD operations

      72 +        String effectiveSortOrder = (sortOrder == null || sortOrder.isBlank())

      74 +        if (!Set.of("asc", "desc").contains(effectiveSortOrder)) {

      79 +        Comparator<Task> comparator = switch (effectiveSortBy) {

      81 +                                   Comparator.nullsLast(Comparator.naturalOrder()));
      82 +            case "priority" -> Comparator.comparingInt((Task t) -> t.getPriority().ordinal());

      94 +                .filter(task -> status   == null || task.getStatus()   == status)
      95 +                .filter(task -> priority == null || task.getPriority() == priority)
      96 +                .sorted(comparator)

  1. TaskController.java

  package com.project.taskmanager.controller;

  import com.project.taskmanager.dto.TaskRequest;
  import com.project.taskmanager.dto.TaskResponse;
  import com.project.taskmanager.model.Priority;
  import com.project.taskmanager.model.Status;
  import com.project.taskmanager.service.TaskService;
  import jakarta.validation.Valid;
  import org.springframework.http.HttpStatus;
  import org.springframework.http.ResponseEntity;
  import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.*;

  import java.util.List;

  @RestController
  @RequestMapping("/tasks")
  public class TaskController {

      private final TaskService taskService;

      public TaskController(TaskService taskService) {
          this.taskService = taskService;
      }

      @GetMapping
      public ResponseEntity<List<TaskResponse>> getAllTasks(
              @RequestParam(required = false) Status status,
              @RequestParam(required = false) Priority priority,
              @RequestParam(required = false) String sortBy,
              @RequestParam(required = false) String sortOrder) {
          return ResponseEntity.ok(taskService.getAllTasks(status, priority, sortBy, sortOrder));
      }

      @GetMapping("/{id}")
      public ResponseEntity<TaskResponse> getTaskById(@PathVariable Long id) {
          return ResponseEntity.ok(taskService.getTaskById(id));
      }

      @PostMapping
      public ResponseEntity<TaskResponse> createTask(@Valid @RequestBody TaskRequest request) {
          return ResponseEntity.status(HttpStatus.CREATED).body(taskService.createTask(request));
      }

      @PutMapping("/{id}")
      public ResponseEntity<TaskResponse> updateTask(@PathVariable Long id,
                                                      @RequestBody TaskRequest request) {
          return ResponseEntity.ok(taskService.updateTask(id, request));
      }

      @DeleteMapping("/{id}")
      public ResponseEntity<Void> deleteTask(@PathVariable Long id) {
          taskService.deleteTask(id);
          return ResponseEntity.noContent().build();
      }
  }

  Changes: Added 4 @RequestParam(required = false) params to getAllTasks(), delegating to the new service overload. Added Priority, Status, RequestParam imports.

  3. app.js

  'use strict';

  // ── State ──────────────────────────────────────────────
  let lastAiSuggestion   = null;
  let editingTaskId      = null;
  let originalEditDate   = null;
  let pendingDeleteId    = null;
  let pendingDeleteTitle = null;
  let successDismissTimer  = null;
  let successDismissTarget = null;

  let currentFilters = { status: '', priority: '', sortBy: 'createdAt', sortOrder: 'desc' };

  // ── Init ───────────────────────────────────────────────
  document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
      loadTasks();

      bindInputClear('title', 'dueDate');
      bindInputClear('edit-title', 'edit-dueDate');
      document.getElementById('ai-desc').addEventListener('input', () => clearFieldError('ai-desc'));

      document.getElementById('edit-modal').addEventListener('click', e => {
          if (e.target === e.currentTarget) closeModal();
      });
      document.getElementById('confirm-modal').addEventListener('click', e => {
          if (e.target === e.currentTarget) closeConfirmModal();
      });

      document.getElementById('task-body').addEventListener('click', e => {
          const btn = e.target.closest('button[data-action]');
          if (!btn) return;
          const id     = parseInt(btn.dataset.id, 10);
          const action = btn.dataset.action;
          if (action === 'edit')   openEditModal(id);
          if (action === 'delete') deleteTask(id, btn.dataset.title);
      });
  });

  function bindInputClear(...ids) {
      ids.forEach(id =>
          document.getElementById(id)?.addEventListener('input', () => clearFieldError(id)));
  }

  // ── Field-error helpers ────────────────────────────────
  function showFieldError(id, message) {
      const el = document.getElementById('err-' + id);
      if (el) el.textContent = message;
  }

  function clearFieldError(id) {
      const el = document.getElementById('err-' + id);
      if (el) el.textContent = '';
  }

  function clearFormErrors(prefix) {
      const p = prefix ? prefix + '-' : '';
      ['title', 'dueDate'].forEach(f => clearFieldError(p + f));
  }

  // ── Validation ─────────────────────────────────────────
  function validateForm(prefix, originalDueDate = null) {
      let valid = true;
      const p   = prefix ? prefix + '-' : '';

      const title = document.getElementById(p + 'title').value.trim();
      if (!title) {
          showFieldError(p + 'title', 'Title is required.');
          valid = false;
      }

      const dueDate = document.getElementById(p + 'dueDate').value;
      if (!dueDate) {
          showFieldError(p + 'dueDate', 'Due date is required.');
          valid = false;
      } else {
          const changed = originalDueDate === null || dueDate !== originalDueDate;
          if (changed && new Date(dueDate) <= new Date()) {
              showFieldError(p + 'dueDate', 'Due date must be in the future.');
              valid = false;
          }
      }

      return valid;
  }

  // ── Task List ──────────────────────────────────────────
  async function loadTasks() {
      try {
          const params = new URLSearchParams();
          if (currentFilters.status)    params.set('status',    currentFilters.status);
          if (currentFilters.priority)  params.set('priority',  currentFilters.priority);
          if (currentFilters.sortBy)    params.set('sortBy',    currentFilters.sortBy);
          if (currentFilters.sortOrder) params.set('sortOrder', currentFilters.sortOrder);

          const query = params.toString() ? '?' + params.toString() : '';
          const res   = await fetch('/tasks' + query);
          const tasks = await res.json();
          renderTasks(tasks);
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('task-msg', 'err', 'Failed to load tasks: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  function applyFilters() {
      currentFilters = {
          status:    document.getElementById('filter-status').value,
          priority:  document.getElementById('filter-priority').value,
          sortBy:    document.getElementById('filter-sortBy').value,
          sortOrder: document.getElementById('filter-sortOrder').value
      };
      loadTasks();
  }

  function clearFilters() {
      currentFilters = { status: '', priority: '', sortBy: 'createdAt', sortOrder: 'desc' };
      document.getElementById('filter-status').value    = '';
      document.getElementById('filter-priority').value  = '';
      document.getElementById('filter-sortBy').value    = 'createdAt';
      document.getElementById('filter-sortOrder').value = 'desc';
      loadTasks();
  }

  function renderTasks(tasks) {
      const tbody = document.getElementById('task-body');
      tbody.innerHTML = '';

      if (!tasks.length) {
          tbody.innerHTML = '<tr class="empty-row"><td colspan="8">No tasks yet. Create one below.</td></tr>';
          return;
      }

      tasks.forEach(t => {
          const tr = document.createElement('tr');
          tr.innerHTML = `
              <td>${t.id}</td>
              <td>${esc(t.title)}</td>
              <td class="col-desc" title="${attr(t.description || '')}">${esc(t.description || '')}</td>
              <td>${fmtDate(t.dueDate)}</td>
              <td><span class="badge badge-${t.priority}">${t.priority}</span></td>
              <td><span class="task-status status-${t.status}">${t.status.replace('_', ' ')}</span></td>
              <td class="col-created">${fmtDate(t.createdAt)}</td>
              <td class="col-actions">
                  <div class="action-btns">
                      <button class="btn btn-sm btn-edit"
                              data-action="edit" data-id="${t.id}">Edit</button>
                      <button class="btn btn-sm btn-delete"
                              data-action="delete" data-id="${t.id}"
                              data-title="${attr(t.title)}">Delete</button>
                  </div>
              </td>`;
          tbody.appendChild(tr);
      });
  }

  // ── Create Task ────────────────────────────────────────
  async function createTask(event) {
      event.preventDefault();
      clearAlert('task-msg');
      clearAlert('create-msg');
      clearFormErrors('');

      if (!validateForm('')) return;

      const payload = {
          title:       document.getElementById('title').value.trim(),
          description: document.getElementById('description').value.trim() || null,
          dueDate:     document.getElementById('dueDate').value,
          priority:    document.getElementById('priority').value,
          status:      document.getElementById('status').value
      };

      try {
          const res  = await fetch('/tasks', {
              method: 'POST',
              headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
              body: JSON.stringify(payload)
          });
          const data = await res.json();
          if (res.ok) {
              showAlert('create-msg', 'ok', 'Task created (ID: ' + data.id + ')');
              document.getElementById('create-form').reset();
              clearFormErrors('');
              loadTasks();
          } else {
              showAlert('create-msg', 'err', formatApiError(data));
          }
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('create-msg', 'err', 'Request failed: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  function resetCreateForm() {
      document.getElementById('create-form').reset();
      clearAlert('create-msg');
      clearFormErrors('');
  }

  // ── Edit Task ──────────────────────────────────────────
  async function openEditModal(id) {
      editingTaskId    = id;
      originalEditDate = null;
      clearFormErrors('edit');
      clearAlert('edit-form-msg');

      try {
          const res = await fetch('/tasks/' + id);
          if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Task not found');
          const task = await res.json();

          originalEditDate = task.dueDate ? task.dueDate.substring(0, 16) : '';

          document.getElementById('edit-title').value       = task.title || '';
          document.getElementById('edit-description').value = task.description || '';
          document.getElementById('edit-dueDate').value     = originalEditDate;
          document.getElementById('edit-priority').value    = task.priority || 'MEDIUM';
          document.getElementById('edit-status').value      = task.status   || 'TODO';

          document.getElementById('edit-modal').showModal();
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('task-msg', 'err', 'Could not open task for editing: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  async function saveEdit(event) {
      event.preventDefault();
      clearFormErrors('edit');

      if (!validateForm('edit', originalEditDate)) return;

      const payload = {
          title:       document.getElementById('edit-title').value.trim(),
          description: document.getElementById('edit-description').value.trim() || null,
          dueDate:     document.getElementById('edit-dueDate').value,
          priority:    document.getElementById('edit-priority').value,
          status:      document.getElementById('edit-status').value
      };

      try {
          const res  = await fetch('/tasks/' + editingTaskId, {
              method: 'PUT',
              headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
              body: JSON.stringify(payload)
          });
          const data = await res.json();
          if (res.ok) {
              closeModal();
              showAlert('task-msg', 'ok', 'Task updated successfully.');
              loadTasks();
          } else {
              showAlert('edit-form-msg', 'err', formatApiError(data));
          }
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('edit-form-msg', 'err', 'Request failed: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  function closeModal() {
      document.getElementById('edit-modal').close();
      editingTaskId    = null;
      originalEditDate = null;
  }

  // ── Delete Task ────────────────────────────────────────
  function deleteTask(id, title) {
      clearAllAlerts();
      pendingDeleteId    = id;
      pendingDeleteTitle = title;
      document.getElementById('confirm-msg').textContent =
          `Are you sure you want to delete "${title}"? This action cannot be undone.`;
      document.getElementById('confirm-modal').showModal();
  }

  async function confirmDelete() {
      if (!pendingDeleteId) return;
      const id    = pendingDeleteId;
      const title = pendingDeleteTitle;
      closeConfirmModal();

      try {
          const res = await fetch('/tasks/' + id, { method: 'DELETE' });
          if (res.ok) {
              showAlert('task-msg', 'ok', `Task "${title}" deleted.`);
              loadTasks();
          } else {
              const data = await res.json();
              showAlert('task-msg', 'err', formatApiError(data));
          }
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('task-msg', 'err', 'Request failed: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  function closeConfirmModal() {
      document.getElementById('confirm-modal').close();
      pendingDeleteId    = null;
      pendingDeleteTitle = null;
  }

  // ── AI Suggestion ──────────────────────────────────────
  async function suggestTask() {
      const desc     = document.getElementById('ai-desc').value.trim();
      const resultEl = document.getElementById('ai-result');
      clearAlert('ai-msg');
      clearFieldError('ai-desc');
      resultEl.style.display = 'none';
      lastAiSuggestion = null;

      if (!desc) {
          showFieldError('ai-desc', 'Description is required.');
          return;
      }

      showAlert('ai-msg', 'info', 'Asking AI…');

      try {
          const res  = await fetch('/tasks/suggest', {
              method: 'POST',
              headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
              body: JSON.stringify({ description: desc })
          });
          const data = await res.json();
          if (res.ok) {
              clearAlert('ai-msg');
              lastAiSuggestion = data.suggestedTask;
              document.getElementById('ai-result-text').textContent = JSON.stringify(data, null, 2);
              resultEl.style.display = 'block';
          } else {
              showAlert('ai-msg', 'err', formatApiError(data));
          }
      } catch (err) {
          showAlert('ai-msg', 'err', 'Request failed: ' + err.message);
      }
  }

  function useAiSuggestion() {
      if (!lastAiSuggestion) return;
      const s = lastAiSuggestion;
      document.getElementById('title').value       = s.title       || '';
      document.getElementById('description').value = s.description || '';
      document.getElementById('dueDate').value     = s.dueDate ? s.dueDate.substring(0, 16) : '';
      document.getElementById('priority').value    = s.priority || 'MEDIUM';
      document.getElementById('status').value      = s.status   || 'TODO';
      clearAlert('create-msg');
      clearFormErrors('');
      document.getElementById('ai-result').style.display = 'none';
      document.getElementById('create-section').scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
  }

  // ── Alert helpers ──────────────────────────────────────
  function showAlert(id, type, text) {
      if (successDismissTimer && successDismissTarget === id) {
          clearTimeout(successDismissTimer);
          successDismissTimer  = null;
          successDismissTarget = null;
      }
      const el = document.getElementById(id);
      if (!el) return;
      el.className = 'alert' +
          (type === 'ok'   ? ' alert-ok'   :
           type === 'err'  ? ' alert-err'  :
           type === 'info' ? ' alert-info' : '');
      el.textContent = text;
      if (type === 'ok') {
          successDismissTarget = id;
          successDismissTimer  = setTimeout(() => {
              clearAlert(id);
              successDismissTimer  = null;
              successDismissTarget = null;
          }, 5000);
      }
  }

  function clearAlert(id) {
      const el = document.getElementById(id);
      if (!el) return;
      el.className   = 'alert';
      el.textContent = '';
  }

  function clearAllAlerts() {
      if (successDismissTimer) {
          clearTimeout(successDismissTimer);
          successDismissTimer  = null;
          successDismissTarget = null;
      }
      ['task-msg', 'create-msg', 'ai-msg', 'edit-form-msg'].forEach(id => clearAlert(id));
  }

  // ── API error formatter ────────────────────────────────
  function formatApiError(data) {
      if (data.errors) {
          return 'Validation errors — ' + Object.entries(data.errors)
              .map(([f, m]) => f + ': ' + m).join(' | ');
      }
      return data.message || 'An unexpected error occurred.';
  }

  // ── DOM / string utils ─────────────────────────────────
  function fmtDate(iso) {
      return iso ? iso.substring(0, 19).replace('T', ' ') : '';
  }

  function esc(text) {
      const d = document.createElement('div');
      d.appendChild(document.createTextNode(String(text)));
      return d.innerHTML;
  }

  function attr(text) {
      return String(text)
          .replace(/&/g, '&amp;')
          .replace(/"/g, '&quot;')
          .replace(/</g, '&lt;')
          .replace(/>/g, '&gt;');
  }

  Changes: Added currentFilters state variable; loadTasks() now builds a URLSearchParams query from it; added applyFilters() and clearFilters() functions. Everything else is unchanged.

  5. TaskControllerIntegrationTest.java

  package com.project.taskmanager.controller;

  import com.project.taskmanager.dto.TaskRequest;
  import com.project.taskmanager.model.Priority;
  import com.project.taskmanager.model.Status;
  import com.project.taskmanager.repository.TaskRepository;
  import org.junit.jupiter.api.BeforeEach;
  import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
  import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
  import org.springframework.boot.test.context.SpringBootTest;
  import org.springframework.boot.test.web.client.TestRestTemplate;
  import org.springframework.http.HttpEntity;
  import org.springframework.http.HttpMethod;
  import org.springframework.http.HttpStatus;
  import org.springframework.http.ResponseEntity;
  import org.springframework.test.context.TestPropertySource;

  import java.time.LocalDateTime;
  import java.util.List;
  import java.util.Map;

  import static org.junit.jupiter.api.Assertions.*;

  @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
  @SpringBootTest(webEnvironment = SpringBootTest.WebEnvironment.RANDOM_PORT)
  @TestPropertySource(properties = "gemini.api.key=test-key")
  class TaskControllerIntegrationTest {

      @Autowired
      private TestRestTemplate restTemplate;

      @Autowired
      private TaskRepository taskRepository;

      private LocalDateTime futureDate;

      @BeforeEach
      void setUp() {
          taskRepository.deleteAll();
          futureDate = LocalDateTime.now().plusDays(30).withNano(0);
      }

      @Test
      void createTask_Returns201WithBody() {
          TaskRequest request = new TaskRequest("Integration Task", "Description", futureDate, Priority.HIGH, null);

          ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", request, Map.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.CREATED, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody().get("id"));
          assertEquals("Integration Task", response.getBody().get("title"));
          assertEquals("HIGH", response.getBody().get("priority"));
          assertEquals("TODO", response.getBody().get("status"));
      }

      @Test
      void getAllTasks_Returns200WithList() {
          TaskRequest request = new TaskRequest("List Task", null, futureDate, Priority.LOW, null);
          restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", request, Map.class);

          ResponseEntity<List> response = restTemplate.getForEntity("/tasks", List.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.OK, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertEquals(1, response.getBody().size());
      }

      @Test
      void getTaskById_Returns200WithTask() {
          TaskRequest request = new TaskRequest("Single Task", null, futureDate, Priority.MEDIUM, null);
          ResponseEntity<Map> created = restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", request, Map.class);
          Number id = (Number) created.getBody().get("id");

          ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate.getForEntity("/tasks/" + id.longValue(), Map.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.OK, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertEquals("Single Task", response.getBody().get("title"));
          assertEquals(id.intValue(), response.getBody().get("id"));
      }

      @Test
      void updateTask_Returns200WithUpdatedData() {
          TaskRequest create = new TaskRequest("Original Task", null, futureDate, Priority.LOW, null);
          ResponseEntity<Map> created = restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", create, Map.class);
          Number id = (Number) created.getBody().get("id");

          TaskRequest update = new TaskRequest("Updated Task", "New desc", futureDate.plusDays(10), Priority.HIGH, null);
          HttpEntity<TaskRequest> updateEntity = new HttpEntity<>(update);

          ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate.exchange(
                  "/tasks/" + id.longValue(), HttpMethod.PUT, updateEntity, Map.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.OK, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertEquals("Updated Task", response.getBody().get("title"));
          assertEquals("HIGH", response.getBody().get("priority"));
      }

      @Test
      void deleteTask_Returns204() {
          TaskRequest request = new TaskRequest("Task to Delete", null, futureDate, Priority.LOW, null);
          ResponseEntity<Map> created = restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", request, Map.class);
          Number id = (Number) created.getBody().get("id");

          ResponseEntity<Void> deleteResponse = restTemplate.exchange(
                  "/tasks/" + id.longValue(), HttpMethod.DELETE, null, Void.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.NO_CONTENT, deleteResponse.getStatusCode());
      }

      @Test
      void getTaskById_NonExistentId_Returns404WithMessage() {
          ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate.getForEntity("/tasks/999", Map.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertEquals(404, response.getBody().get("status"));
          assertTrue(((String) response.getBody().get("message")).contains("999"));
      }

      @Test
      void createTask_BlankTitle_Returns400WithFieldError() {
          TaskRequest request = new TaskRequest("", "Description", futureDate, Priority.HIGH, null);

          ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks", request, Map.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.BAD_REQUEST, response.getStatusCode());
          assertNotNull(response.getBody());
          assertEquals(400, response.getBody().get("status"));
          Map<String, String> errors = (Map<String, String>) response.getBody().get("errors");
          assertNotNull(errors);
          assertTrue(errors.containsKey("title"));
      }

      @Test
      void getAllTasks_FilterByStatus_ReturnsOnlyMatchingTasks() {
          restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks",
              new TaskRequest("Todo Task", null, futureDate, Priority.MEDIUM, Status.TODO), Map.class);
          restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks",
              new TaskRequest("Done Task", null, futureDate, Priority.LOW, Status.DONE), Map.class);

          ResponseEntity<List> response = restTemplate.getForEntity("/tasks?status=TODO", List.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.OK, response.getStatusCode());
          assertEquals(1, response.getBody().size());
          Map<String, Object> task = (Map<String, Object>) response.getBody().get(0);
          assertEquals("TODO", task.get("status"));
          assertEquals("Todo Task", task.get("title"));
      }

      @Test
      void getAllTasks_SortByDueDateAscending_ReturnsInChronologicalOrder() {
          LocalDateTime nearDate = futureDate;
          LocalDateTime farDate  = futureDate.plusDays(60);
          restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks",
              new TaskRequest("Far Task",  null, farDate,  Priority.LOW, null), Map.class);
          restTemplate.postForEntity("/tasks",
              new TaskRequest("Near Task", null, nearDate, Priority.LOW, null), Map.class);

          ResponseEntity<List> response = restTemplate.getForEntity(
              "/tasks?sortBy=dueDate&sortOrder=asc", List.class);

          assertEquals(HttpStatus.OK, response.getStatusCode());
          assertEquals(2, response.getBody().size());
          assertEquals("Near Task", ((Map<?, ?>) response.getBody().get(0)).get("title"));
          assertEquals("Far Task",  ((Map<?, ?>) response.getBody().get(1)).get("title"));
      }
  }

  Changes: Added import com.project.taskmanager.model.Status; and two new test methods at the bottom. All 7 existing tests are byte-for-byte identical.
